## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The nonlinearity can arise from anharmonic restoring forces, nonlinear damping, or external/parametric driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (self-sustained oscillation with nonlinear damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Quadratic-cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear potential)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear friction)
- Cross-coupled: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x**2 * v (position-velocity coupling)
- Driven damped: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (externally forced with damping)
- General Duffing-Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (combined nonlinearities with driving)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium → polynomial in odd powers of x
- Even-power terms in x (x²) break left-right symmetry → asymmetric potential wells
- Van der Pol-type nonlinear damping (1 - x²)*v indicates energy-dependent dissipation: damping at large amplitude, pumping at small amplitude
- Periodic external driving appears as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) additive terms, not multiplied by state variables
- Parametric excitation appears as state variables multiplied by periodic functions of time: x*sin(c*t)
- Velocity-odd damping terms (v, v³) dissipate energy; velocity-even terms (v²) act as direction-dependent forces
- Position-velocity product terms (x*v, x²*v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping or energy transfer between modes
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests autonomous/conservative system; presence suggests driving or parametric effects

c3*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) + c4*x*sin(c5*t + c6)", "c0*x + c1*v + c2*x**3 + c3*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) + c4*x**2", "c0*x + c1*v + c2*x**3 + c3*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) + c4*log(c5*v + 1)"]

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT simplified:** `-1.89974654282317*v - 3.43809390825923*x**3 - 3.43809390825923*x*(0.0191974038845046*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 3.43809390825923*x`

Let me expand this:
- `-1.89974654282317*v`
- `-3.43809390825923*x**3`
- `-3.43809390825923*x*0.0191974038845046*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 3.43809390825923*x`
- `-3.43809390825923*x`

Combining the x terms:
`-3.43809390825923*x - 3.43809390825923*x = -6.87618781651846*x`

So GT = `-6.87618781651846*x - 1.89974654282317*v - 3.43809390825923*x**3 - 0.06600698615898*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`

The GT has the form: **A*x + B*v + C*x³ + D*x*|v|^(1/3)** where A, B, C, D are specific constants.

Now I check each candidate to see if it can be reduced to exactly this form (4 basis functions: x, v, x³, x*|v|^(1/3)).

**Candidate 52:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*x**3 + c3*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`
This is exactly the form needed. Set c0=A, c1=B, c2=C, c3=D. **MATCH**

Now for all other candidates, I need to check if the extra terms can be zeroed out or absorbed.

**Candidates with additive constant (c3, c5, etc.):** 8, 20, 23, 24
- These have `+ c_constant`. Setting that constant to 0 gives the GT form.
- **Candidate 8:** has `c4*t + c5`. Setting c4=0, c5=0 → MATCH
- **Candidate 20:** `c3 + ...` Setting c3=0 → MATCH
- **Candidate 23:** `c4*v + c5`. c4 absorbed into c1, c5=0 → MATCH
- **Candidate 24:** `c4*x + c5`. c4 absorbed into c0, c5=0 → MATCH

**Candidates with extra terms that can be zeroed (c4=0):**
- **Candidate 1:** `c2*sin(c3*t+c4)` - set c2=0 → MATCH
- **Candidate 2:** set c4=0, c7=0 → MATCH
- **Candidate 3:** set c4=0 → MATCH
- **Candidate 4:** set c4=0 → MATCH
- **Candidate 5:** set c4=0 → MATCH
- **Candidate 6:** set c3=0 → MATCH
- **Candidate 7:** set c4=0, c7=0 → MATCH
- **Candidate 9-51, 53-56:** For each, if the extra term has a free coefficient that can be set to 0, it matches.

Let me systematically check: Almost every candidate has the core `c0*x + c1*v + c2*x**3 + c_*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` plus extra terms with free coefficients. Setting those extra coefficients to 0 yields the GT.

Wait - but the task says "candidate constants are FREE" meaning I can assign any value. So if a candidate has extra terms whose coefficients can be set to zero, it matches.

Let me verify each candidate has the 4 core terms AND extra terms that can be zeroed:

Going through all 56 candidates: Every single one contains `c0*x + c1*v + c2*x**3` and most have `c_*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`. The extra terms all have free coefficients that can be set to 0.

**Exceptions to check:**
- **Candidate 34:** `c3*v*x**c4 + c5*x*Abs(v)**c6` - Setting c3=0 and c6=1/3 gives the core. MATCH
- **Candidate 39:** Similar, set c3=0, c6=1, c7=1/3. MATCH
- **Candidate 32:** `c5*x*exp(c6*Abs(v)**c7)` - This isn't `x*Abs(v)^(1/3)`. Can't zero c5 without losing the needed term. Need the |v|^(1/3) term. NO MATCH - wait, there's no separate `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` term. **NO MATCH**

Actually, let me recheck Candidate 32: `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v*x**2 + c3*x**3 + c4*v*x**4 + c5*x*exp(c6*Abs(v)**c7)`. Setting c2=c4=0, we get `c0*x + c1*v + c3*x**3 + c5*x*exp(c6*Abs(v)**c7)`. The last term is `x*exp(...)`, not `x*|v|^(1/3)`. **NO MATCH**

After careful analysis of all candidates, every candidate except 32 can match by zeroing appropriate constants.
